Barter,\n\nNoise\n\nand\n\nIndiana\n\nArea\n\nof Interest\n\n14.3\n\nReduction\n\nAcknowledgments\n\nThe authors\nthank Dr. N. Saiyed and Dr. J. Bridges of NASA Lewis (now NASA Glenn) for their significant\nefforts\nin program\ncoordination,\ntest planning,\ntest conduct,\nand data processing.\nThe authors\nalso acknowledge\nJ.F. Brausch, R.S. Coffin, and B.R. Delaney\nof GE Aircraft Engines and F. Smith and Dr. B.R. Vittal of\nAllison Engine Company\nfor technical\nsupport\nand unique\ncontributions\nto this program\neffort.\n\nthat\n\nat the time of research,\n\nNASA\nI Note\n\nAvailable\nNASA Center\n7121 Standard\n\nfor Aerospace\nDrive\n\nthe NASA\n\nLewis\n\nResearch\n\nwas undergoing\na name change to the\nJohn H. Glenn Research\nCenter at Lewis\nBoth names may appear in this report.\n\nField.\n\nfrom\nNational\n\nInformation\n\nCenter\n\nTechnical\n\nInformation\n\nService\n\n5285 Port Royal Road\nSpringfield,\nVA 22100\nPrice Code: A13\n\nHanover,\nMD 21076\nPrice Code: A13\nAvailable\n\nelectronically\n\nat http: //gltrs.grc.nasa.gov/GLTRS\n\nPREFACE\nIn 1995, NASA GRC initiated efforts to meet the US industry\'s rising need to develop jet noise technology for separate flow nozzle exhaust systems. Such technology would be applicable to long-range aircraft\nusing medium to high by-pass ratio engines. With support from the Advanced Subsonic Technology Noise\nReduction program, these efforts resulted in the formulation of an experimental study, the Separate Flow\nNozzle Test (SFNT). SFNT\'s objectives were to develop a data base on various by-pass ratio nozzles,\nscreen quietest configurations and acquire pertinent data for predicting the plume behavior and ultimately\nits corresponding\njet noise. The SFNT was a team effort between NASA GRC\'s various divisions, NASA\nLangley, General Electric, Pratt&Whitney,\nUnited Technologies Research Corporation, Allison Engine\nCompany, Boeing, ASE FluiDyne, MicroCraft, Eagle Aeronautics and Combustion Research and Flow\nTechnology Incorporated.\nSFNT found several exhaust systems providing over 2.5 EPNdB reduction at take-off with less than 0.5%\nthrust loss at cruise with simulated flight speed of 0.8 Mach. Please see the following SFNT related\nreports: Saiyed, et al. (NASA/T_2000-209948),\nSaiyed, et al. (NASA/C_2000-210524),\nLow, et al. (NASA/CRY000-210040),\nJanardan et al. (NASA/CR\n2000-210039),\nBobbitt, et al.\n(NASA/CR\n201-210706) and Kenzakowski et al. (NASA/C_2001-210611.).\nI wish to thank the entire SFNT team of nearly 50 scientists, engineers, technicians and programmers\ninvolved in this project. SFNT would have fallen well short of its goals without their untiring support,\ndedication to developing the jet noise technology.\nNaseem Saiyed\nSFNT
